      <p><b>Brunei</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">uː</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Brunei.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/19/En-us-Brunei.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Brunei.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">broo-<span style="font-size:90%">NY</span></i></a>; <small>Malay:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Malay" title="Help:IPA/Malay">[brunaɪ]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brunei-pronunciation-ms.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/05/Brunei-pronunciation-ms.ogg" class="internal" title="Brunei-pronunciation-ms.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>), officially the <b>Nation of Brunei, the Abode of Peace</b><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>: <i lang="ms">Negara Brunei Darussalam</i>, <a href="/wiki/Jawi_alphabet" title="Jawi alphabet">Jawi</a>: <span lang="ms-Arab" dir="rtl" title="Malay (macrolanguage)-language text">نڬارا بروني دارالسلام</span>‎), is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">country</a> located on the north coast of the island of <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>. Apart from its coastline with the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>, the country is completely surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysian</a> <a href="/wiki/Federated_state" title="Federated state">state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a>. It is separated into two parts by the Sarawak district of <a href="/wiki/Limbang_District" title="Limbang District">Limbang</a>. Brunei is the only sovereign state completely on the island of Borneo; the remainder of the island's territory is divided between the nations of Malaysia and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Brunei" title="Demographics of Brunei">Brunei's population</a> was 428,963 in 2018. The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Brunei" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Brunei">government</a> is an absolute monarchy under the <a href="/wiki/Sultan_of_Brunei" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultan of Brunei">Sultan</a>, which implements a combination of <a href="/wiki/English_common_law" class="mw-redirect" title="English common law">English common law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sharia_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharia law">sharia law</a>, as well as direct general <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islamic</a> practices. </p>
      <p>At the peak of the <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Empire" title="Bruneian Empire">Bruneian Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolkiah" title="Bolkiah">Sultan Bolkiah</a> (reigned 1485–1528) is alleged to have had control over most regions of <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a>, including modern-day Sarawak and <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Sulu_Archipelago" title="Sulu Archipelago">Sulu Archipelago</a> off the northeast tip of Borneo, and the islands off the northwest tip of Borneo. Claims also state that they had control over <a href="/wiki/Seludong" class="mw-redirect" title="Seludong">Seludong</a> ("<b>Kingdom of Maynila</b>" to the local rulers of Maynila; where modern-day <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a> now stands) but Southeast Asian scholars believe this refers to a settlement Mount Selurong in Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-Abinales2005_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abinales2005-11">[11]</a></sup> For political reasons, the historical rulers of Maynila maintained close cognatic ties through intermarriage with the ruling houses of the <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Empire" title="Bruneian Empire">Sultanate of Brunei</a>, but Brunei's political influence over Maynila is not considered to have extended to military or political rule.<sup id="cite_ref-Junker1998_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Junker1998-12">[12]</a></sup> Intermarriage was a common strategy for large <a href="/wiki/Thalassocracy" title="Thalassocracy">thalassocratic states</a> (maritime states) such as Brunei to extend their influence, and for local rulers such as those of Maynila to help strengthen their family claims to nobility.<sup id="cite_ref-Scott1994_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scott1994-13">[13]</a></sup> The maritime state of Brunei was visited by Spain's <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Magellan%27s_circumnavigation" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of Magellan's circumnavigation">Magellan Expedition</a> in 1521 and fought against Spain in the 1578 <a href="/wiki/Castilian_War" title="Castilian War">Castilian War</a>. </p>
      <p>During the 19th century, the Bruneian Empire began to decline. The Sultanate ceded Sarawak (<a href="/wiki/Kuching" title="Kuching">Kuching</a>) to <a href="/wiki/James_Brooke" title="James Brooke">James Brooke</a> and installed him as the <a href="/wiki/White_Rajahs" title="White Rajahs">White Rajah</a>, and it ceded Sabah to the British <a href="/wiki/North_Borneo_Chartered_Company" title="North Borneo Chartered Company">North Borneo Chartered Company</a>. In 1888, Brunei became a <a href="/wiki/British_protectorate" title="British protectorate">British protectorate</a> and was assigned a <a href="/wiki/Resident_(title)" class="mw-redirect" title="Resident (title)">British resident</a> as colonial manager in 1906. After the Japanese occupation during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, in 1959 a new constitution was written. In 1962, a small <a href="/wiki/Brunei_revolt" title="Brunei revolt">armed rebellion</a> against the monarchy was ended with the help of the British. </p>
      <p>Brunei gained its independence from the United Kingdom on 1 January 1984. Economic growth during the 1990s and 2000s, with the GDP increasing 56% from 1999 to 2008, transformed Brunei into an industrialised country. It has developed wealth from extensive petroleum and natural gas fields. Brunei has the second-highest <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeast Asian">Southeast Asian</a> nations, after <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, and is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), Brunei is ranked fifth in the world by gross domestic product per capita at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>. The IMF estimated in 2011 that Brunei was one of two countries (the other being <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>) with a public debt at 0% of the national GDP. </p>

        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Politics_and_government"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Politics and government</span></a>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
      <p>According to local historiography, Brunei was founded by Awang Alak Betatar, later to be <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Shah_of_Brunei" title="Muhammad Shah of Brunei">Sultan Muhammad Shah</a>, reigning around AD 1400. He moved from Garang in the <a href="/wiki/Temburong" class="mw-redirect" title="Temburong">Temburong</a> District<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200926_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200926-14">[14]</a></sup> to the <a href="/wiki/Brunei_River" title="Brunei River">Brunei River</a> estuary, discovering Brunei. According to legend, upon landing he exclaimed, <i>Baru nah</i> (loosely translated as "that's it!" or "there"), from which the name "Brunei" was derived.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEde_Vienne201627_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_Vienne201627-15">[15]</a></sup> He was the first Muslim ruler of Brunei.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Before the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Empire" title="Bruneian Empire">Bruneian Empire</a> under the Muslim Bolkiah Dynasty, Brunei is believed to have been under Buddhist rulers.<sup id="cite_ref-Nicholl1980_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nicholl1980-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It was renamed "Barunai" in the 14th century, possibly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> word "<i><i lang="sa-Latn" title="Sanskrit-language romanization">varuṇ</i></i>" (<span lang="sa" title="Sanskrit-language text">वरुण</span>), meaning "seafarers".<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan2012_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan2012-18">[18]</a></sup> The word "<a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a>" is of the same origin. In the country's full name, <i><i lang="ms" title="Malay (macrolanguage)-language text">Negara Brunei Darussalam</i></i>, <i><i lang="ms" title="Malay (macrolanguage)-language text">darussalam</i></i> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">دار السلام</span>‎) means "abode of peace", while <i><i lang="ms" title="Malay (macrolanguage)-language text">negara</i></i> means "country" in <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>. </p>
      <p>The earliest recorded documentation by the West about Brunei is by an Italian known as <a href="/wiki/Ludovico_di_Varthema" title="Ludovico di Varthema">Ludovico di Varthema</a>, who also said the "Bruneian people have fairer skin tone than the peoples he met in <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku Islands</a>". On his documentation back to 1550; </p> 
      <blockquote>
       <p>We arrived at the island of Bornei<i> (Brunei or Borneo), </i>which is distant from the <i>Maluch</i> about two hundred miles [three hundred kilometres], and we found that it was somewhat larger than the aforesaid and much lower. The people are pagans and are men of goodwill. Their colour is whiter than that of the other sort&nbsp;... in this island justice is well administered&nbsp;...<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brunei" title="History of Brunei">History of Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span></h3> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992277484">.mw-parser-output .stack-container{box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .stack-clear-left{float:left;clear:left}.mw-parser-output .stack-clear-right{float:right;clear:right}.mw-parser-output .stack-left{float:left}.mw-parser-output .stack-right{float:right}.mw-parser-output .stack-margin-clear-left{float:left;clear:left;margin-right:1em}.mw-parser-output .stack-margin-clear-right{float:right;clear:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .stack-margin-left{float:left;margin-right:1em}.mw-parser-output .stack-margin-right{float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .stack-container>div{margin:1px;overflow:hidden}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .stack-container{float:none;width:100%}}</style>
      <div class="mw-stack stack-container stack-left">
       <div>
        <div class="thumb tleft">
         <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Tomb_of_the_King_of_Boni_(Brunei)_Nanjing.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/The_Tomb_of_the_King_of_Boni_%28Brunei%29_Nanjing.JPG/220px-The_Tomb_of_the_King_of_Boni_%28Brunei%29_Nanjing.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/The_Tomb_of_the_King_of_Boni_%28Brunei%29_Nanjing.JPG/330px-The_Tomb_of_the_King_of_Boni_%28Brunei%29_Nanjing.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/The_Tomb_of_the_King_of_Boni_%28Brunei%29_Nanjing.JPG/440px-The_Tomb_of_the_King_of_Boni_%28Brunei%29_Nanjing.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <div class="magnify">
            <a href="/wiki/File:The_Tomb_of_the_King_of_Boni_(Brunei)_Nanjing.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
           </div>The <a href="/wiki/Tomb_of_the_King_of_Boni" title="Tomb of the King of Boni">tomb of a ruler of Boni</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jiangsu" title="Jiangsu">Jiangsu</a>, China
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The settlement known as Vijayapura was a colony to the Buddhist <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Srivijaya</a> empire and was thought to be located in Borneo's Northwest which flourished in the 7th Century.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In the aftermath of the Indian <a href="/wiki/Chola_invasion_of_Srivijaya" title="Chola invasion of Srivijaya">Chola invasion of Srivijaya</a>, Datu Puti lead some dissident datus from Sumatra and Borneo in a rebellion against Rajah Makatunao who was a Chola appointed local Rajah. The dissidents and their retinue tried to revive Srivijaya in a new country called <a href="/wiki/Kedatuan_of_Madja-as" class="mw-redirect" title="Kedatuan of Madja-as">Madja-as</a> in the Visayas islands (an archipelago named after Srivijaya) in the Philippines. One of the earliest Chinese records of an independent kingdom in Borneo is the 977 AD letter to the Chinese emperor from the ruler of Boni, which some scholars believe to refer to Borneo.<sup id="cite_ref-Hutton2000_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hutton2000-21">[21]</a></sup> In 1225, the Chinese official <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Rukuo" title="Zhao Rukuo">Zhao Rukuo</a> reported that Boni had 100 warships to protect its trade, and that there was great wealth in the kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200943_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200943-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 14th century, the <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Javanese</a> manuscript <i><a href="/wiki/Nagarakretagama" title="Nagarakretagama">Nagarakretagama</a></i>, written by <a href="/wiki/Mpu_Prapanca" title="Mpu Prapanca">Prapanca</a> in 1365, mentioned <i>Barune</i> as the <a href="/wiki/Constituent_state" title="Constituent state">constituent state</a> of Hindu <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> which had to make an annual <a href="/wiki/Tribute" title="Tribute">tribute</a> of 40 <a href="/wiki/Catty" title="Catty">katis</a> of <a href="/wiki/Camphor" title="Camphor">camphor</a>. In 1369, Sulu which was also formerly part of Majapahit, had successfully rebelled and then attacked Boni, looting it of treasure and gold. A fleet from Majapahit succeeded in driving away the Sulus, but Boni was left weaker after the attack.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200944_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200944-24">[24]</a></sup> A Chinese report from 1371 described Boni as poor and totally controlled by Majapahit.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200945_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200945-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the 15th century, Boni had seceded from Majapahit and then converted to Islam. Thus transforming into the independent Sultanate of Brunei. Brunei became a <a href="/wiki/Hashemite" class="mw-redirect" title="Hashemite">Hashemite</a> state when she allowed the Arab Emir of Mecca, <a href="/wiki/Sharif_Ali" title="Sharif Ali">Sharif Ali</a>, to become her third sultan. Scholars claim that the power of the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultanate">Sultanate</a> of Brunei was at <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Empire" title="Bruneian Empire">its peak</a> between the 15th and 17th centuries, with its power extending from northern Borneo to the southern Philippines (Sulu) and even in the northern Philippines (Manila) which Brunei incorporated via territorial acquisition accomplished through royal marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-26">[26]</a></sup> Sultan Bolkiah had extended Brunei's power to its greatest extent when it conquered Manila and Sulu as he even attempted but failed to conquer the Visayas islands even though Sultan Bolkiah was half-Visayan himself being descended from a Visayan mother and he was famously known as Sultan Ragam "The Singing Captain", his powerful musical voice was a trait he inherited from his Visayan lineage since Visayans were culturally obsessed with singing, with the best <a href="/wiki/Madja-as" title="Madja-as">Visayan singers often also being members of their warrior castes too</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> However, Islamic Brunei's power was not uncontested in Borneo since it had a Hindu rival in a state founded by Indians called <a href="/wiki/Kutai" title="Kutai">Kutai</a> in the south which they overpowered but didn't destroy. Brunei's dominance in the Philippines was also challenged by two Indianized kingdoms, the Rajahanates of <a href="/wiki/Rajahnate_of_Cebu" class="mw-redirect" title="Rajahnate of Cebu">Cebu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rajahnate_of_Butuan" class="mw-redirect" title="Rajahnate of Butuan">Butuan</a> which were also coincidentally allied with Kutai and were also at war with Brunei's dependencies; Sulu and Manila as well as their mutual ally, the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Maguindanao" title="Sultanate of Maguindanao">Sultanate of Maguindanao</a>. The Kedatuans of Madja-as and Dapitan were also belligerent against Brunei due to them being the targets of constant Muslim attacks organized from Maguindanao and <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Ternate" title="Sultanate of Ternate">Ternate</a>, a Papuan speaking state in the vicinity of Oceania that grew wealthy by monopolizing spice production. Nevertheless, by the 16th century, Islam was firmly rooted in Brunei, and the country had built one of its biggest mosques. In 1578, Alonso Beltrán, a Spanish traveller, described it as being five stories tall and built on the water.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War_with_Spain_and_decline">War with Spain and decline</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Brunei_territorial_lose_(1400%E2%80%931890).gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Brunei_territorial_lose_%281400%E2%80%931890%29.gif/220px-Brunei_territorial_lose_%281400%E2%80%931890%29.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Brunei_territorial_lose_%281400%E2%80%931890%29.gif/330px-Brunei_territorial_lose_%281400%E2%80%931890%29.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Brunei_territorial_lose_%281400%E2%80%931890%29.gif/440px-Brunei_territorial_lose_%281400%E2%80%931890%29.gif 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="225"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Brunei_territorial_lose_(1400%E2%80%931890).gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Brunei territorial losses from 1400 to 1890
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p> Brunei briefly rose to prominence in Southeast Asia when the Portuguese occupied <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">Malacca</a> and thereby forced the wealthy and powerful but displaced Muslim refugees there to relocate to nearby Sultanates such as <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Aceh" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultanate of Aceh">Aceh</a> and Brunei. However, <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">European influence</a> gradually brought an end to the <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a>, as Brunei entered a period of decline compounded by internal strife over royal succession. In the face of these invasions by European Christian powers, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Caliphate</a> aided the beleaguered Southeast Asian Sultanates by making <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_expedition_to_Aceh" title="Ottoman expedition to Aceh">Aceh</a> a <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> and sending expeditions to reinforce, train and equip the local <a href="/wiki/Mujahideen" title="Mujahideen">mujahideen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Spain <a href="/wiki/Castille_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Castille War">declared war</a> in 1578, planning to attack and capture <a href="/wiki/Kota_Batu,_Brunei-Muara" title="Kota Batu, Brunei-Muara">Kota Batu</a>, Brunei's capital at the time. This was based in part on the assistance of two Bruneian <a href="/wiki/Pengiran#Brunei" class="mw-redirect" title="Pengiran">noblemen</a>, Pengiran Seri Lela and Pengiran Seri Ratna. The former had travelled to <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>, then the centre of the Spanish colony. Manila itself was captured from Brunei, Christianised and made a territory of the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">Viceroyalty of New Spain</a> which was centered in Mexico City. Pengiran Seri Lela came to offer Brunei as a <a href="/wiki/Tributary_state" title="Tributary state">tributary</a> to Spain for help to recover the throne usurped by his brother, Saiful Rijal.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The Spanish agreed that if they succeeded in conquering Brunei, Pengiran Seri Lela would be appointed as the sultan, while Pengiran Seri Ratna would be the new <a href="/wiki/Bendahara" title="Bendahara">Bendahara</a>. </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Control_of_the_island_of_Borneo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Control_of_the_island_of_Borneo.png/220px-Control_of_the_island_of_Borneo.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Control_of_the_island_of_Borneo.png/330px-Control_of_the_island_of_Borneo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Control_of_the_island_of_Borneo.png/440px-Control_of_the_island_of_Borneo.png 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="1202"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Control_of_the_island_of_Borneo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Boundaries of Brunei (green) since 1890
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In March 1578, a fresh Spanish fleet had arrived from Mexico and settled at the Philippines, they were led by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Sande" title="Francisco de Sande">De Sande</a>, acting as <a href="/wiki/Capit%C3%A1n-General" class="mw-redirect" title="Capitán-General">Capitán-General</a>, he organised an expedition from Manila for Brunei. The expedition consisted of 400 Spaniards and Mexicans, 1,500 <a href="/wiki/Filipino_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Filipino people">Filipino</a> natives and 300 Borneans.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The campaign was one of many, which also included action in <a href="/wiki/Mindanao" title="Mindanao">Mindanao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sulu_Archipelago" title="Sulu Archipelago">Sulu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The racial make-up of the Christian side was diverse since it were usually made up of <a href="/wiki/Mestizos" class="mw-redirect" title="Mestizos">Mestizos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mulattoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Mulattoes">Mulattoes</a> and Amerindians (<a href="/wiki/Aztecs" title="Aztecs">Aztecs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayans" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayans">Mayans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Incans" class="mw-redirect" title="Incans">Incans</a>) who were gathered and sent from Mexico and were led by Spanish officers who had worked together with native Filipinos in military campaigns across the Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The Muslim side though was also equally racially diverse. In addition to the native Malay warriors, the Ottomans had repeatedly sent military expeditions to nearby <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_expedition_to_Aceh" title="Ottoman expedition to Aceh">Aceh</a>. The expeditions were composed mainly of <a href="/wiki/Turkic_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkic people">Turks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">Egyptians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">Swahilis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somalis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sindhis" title="Sindhis">Sindhis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gujaratis" class="mw-redirect" title="Gujaratis">Gujaratis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malabars" title="Malabars">Malabars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> These expeditionary forces had also spread to other nearby Sultanates such as Brunei and had taught new fighting tactics and techniques on how to forge cannons.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Eventually, the Spanish invaded the capital on 16 April 1578, with the help of Pengiran Seri Lela and Pengiran Seri Ratna. The Sultan Saiful Rijal and Paduka Seri Begawan Sultan Abdul Kahar were forced to flee to Meragang then to <a href="/wiki/Jerudong" title="Jerudong">Jerudong</a>. In Jerudong, they made plans to chase the conquering army away from Brunei. Suffering high fatalities due to a <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> or <a href="/wiki/Dysentery" title="Dysentery">dysentery</a> outbreak,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> the Spanish decided to abandon Brunei and returned to Manila on 26 June 1578, after 72 days. Before doing so, they burned the mosque, a high structure with a five-tier roof.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Pengiran Seri Lela died in August or September 1578, probably from the same illness suffered by his Spanish allies.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> There was suspicion that he the legitimate Sultan could have been poisoned by the ruling sultan.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Seri Lela's daughter, a Bruneian princess, "Putri", had left with the Spanish, she abandoned her claim to the crown and then she married a Christian <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_people" title="Tagalog people">Tagalog</a>, named Agustín de Legazpi de Tondo.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The local Brunei accounts<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200941_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200941-41">[41]</a></sup> of the Castilian War differ greatly from the generally accepted view of events. What was called the Castilian War was seen as a heroic episode, with the Spaniards being driven out by Bendahara Sakam, purportedly a brother of the ruling sultan, and a thousand native warriors. Most historians consider this to be a <a href="/wiki/Folk-hero" class="mw-redirect" title="Folk-hero">folk-hero</a> account, which probably developed decades or centuries after.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brunei eventually descended into anarchy. The country suffered a <a href="/wiki/Brunei_Civil_War" title="Brunei Civil War">civil war</a> from 1660 to 1673. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_intervention">British intervention</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/British_Brunei_Administrators" class="mw-redirect" title="British Brunei Administrators">British Brunei Administrators</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Borneo" title="British Borneo">British Borneo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Labuan_on_18_December_1846.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/The_signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Labuan_on_18_December_1846.jpg/220px-The_signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Labuan_on_18_December_1846.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/The_signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Labuan_on_18_December_1846.jpg/330px-The_signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Labuan_on_18_December_1846.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/The_signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Labuan_on_18_December_1846.jpg/440px-The_signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Labuan_on_18_December_1846.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="405"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Labuan_on_18_December_1846.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>British adventurer <a href="/wiki/James_Brooke" title="James Brooke">James Brooke</a> negotiating with the <a href="/wiki/Sultan_of_Brunei" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultan of Brunei">Sultan of Brunei</a>, which led to the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Labuan" title="Treaty of Labuan">Treaty of Labuan</a>, 1846
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The British have intervened in the affairs of Brunei on several occasions. Britain attacked Brunei in July 1846 due to internal conflicts over who was the rightful Sultan.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200952_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200952-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 1880s, the decline of the <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Empire" title="Bruneian Empire">Bruneian Empire</a> continued. The sultan granted land (now Sarawak) to <a href="/wiki/James_Brooke" title="James Brooke">James Brooke</a>, who had helped him quell a rebellion and allowed him to establish the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sarawak" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Sarawak">Kingdom of Sarawak</a>. Over time, Brooke and his nephews (who succeeded him) leased or annexed more land. Brunei lost much of its territory to him and his dynasty, known as the <a href="/wiki/White_Rajahs" title="White Rajahs">White Rajahs</a>. </p>
      <p>Sultan <a href="/wiki/Hashim_Jalilul_Alam_Aqamaddin" title="Hashim Jalilul Alam Aqamaddin">Hashim Jalilul Alam Aqamaddin</a> appealed to the British to stop further encroachment by the Brookes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam20093_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam20093-44">[44]</a></sup> The "Treaty of Protection" was negotiated by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Hugh_Low" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Hugh Low">Sir Hugh Low</a> and signed into effect on 17 September 1888. The treaty said that the sultan "could not cede or lease any territory to foreign powers without British consent"; it provided <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a> effective control over Brunei's external affairs, making it a <a href="/wiki/British_protected_state" class="mw-redirect" title="British protected state">British protected state</a> (which continued until 1984).<sup id="cite_ref-cia_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-26">[26]</a></sup> But, when the Kingdom of Sarawak annexed Brunei's <a href="/wiki/Limbang_Division" title="Limbang Division">Pandaruan District</a> in 1890, the British did not take any action to stop it. They did not regard either Brunei or the Kingdom of Sarawak as 'foreign' (per the Treaty of Protection). This final annexation by Sarawak left Brunei with its current small land mass and separation into two parts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200958_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200958-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/British_resident" class="mw-redirect" title="British resident">British residents</a> were introduced in Brunei under the Supplementary Protectorate Agreement in 1906.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200959_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200959-46">[46]</a></sup> The residents were to advise the sultan on all matters of administration. Over time, the resident assumed more executive control than the sultan. The residential system ended in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200967_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200967-47">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery_of_oil">Discovery of oil</span></h3> 
      <p>Petroleum was discovered in 1929 after several fruitless attempts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200912_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200912-48">[48]</a></sup> Two men, F. F. Marriot and T. G. Cochrane, smelled oil near the <a href="/wiki/Seria" title="Seria">Seria</a> river in late 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200913_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200913-49">[49]</a></sup> They informed a <a href="/wiki/Geophysicist" class="mw-redirect" title="Geophysicist">geophysicist</a>, who conducted a survey there. In 1927, gas seepages were reported in the area. Seria Well Number One (S-1) was drilled on 12 July 1928. Oil was struck at 297 metres (974&nbsp;ft) on 5 April 1929. Seria Well Number 2 was drilled on 19 August 1929, and, as of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brunei&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, continues to produce oil.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200914_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200914-50">[50]</a></sup> Oil production was increased considerably in the 1930s with the development of more oil fields. In 1940, oil production was at more than six million barrels.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200914_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200914-50">[50]</a></sup> The British Malayan Petroleum Company (now <a href="/wiki/Brunei_Shell_Petroleum" class="mw-redirect" title="Brunei Shell Petroleum">Brunei Shell Petroleum</a> Company) was formed on 22 July 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200915_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200915-51">[51]</a></sup> The first offshore well was drilled in 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Oil and natural gas have been the basis of Brunei's development and wealth since the late 20th century. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japanese_occupation">Japanese occupation</span></h3> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
