          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_British_Borneo" title="Japanese occupation of British Borneo">Japanese occupation of British Borneo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_Ahmad_Tajuddin_(AWM_P10841.001).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Sultan_Ahmad_Tajuddin_%28AWM_P10841.001%29.JPG/220px-Sultan_Ahmad_Tajuddin_%28AWM_P10841.001%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="296" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Sultan_Ahmad_Tajuddin_%28AWM_P10841.001%29.JPG/330px-Sultan_Ahmad_Tajuddin_%28AWM_P10841.001%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Sultan_Ahmad_Tajuddin_%28AWM_P10841.001%29.JPG/440px-Sultan_Ahmad_Tajuddin_%28AWM_P10841.001%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="474" data-file-height="637"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_Ahmad_Tajuddin_(AWM_P10841.001).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Tajuddin" title="Ahmad Tajuddin">Ahmad Tajuddin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Sultans_of_Brunei" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Sultans of Brunei">27th Sultan of Brunei</a>, with members of his court in April 1941, eight months before the Japanese invaded Brunei
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Japanese invaded Brunei on 16 December 1941, eight days after their <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a> and the United States Navy. They landed 10,000 troops of the <a href="/wiki/Kawaguchi_Detachment" title="Kawaguchi Detachment">Kawaguchi Detachment</a> from <a href="/wiki/Cam_Ranh_Bay" title="Cam Ranh Bay">Cam Ranh Bay</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Belait" title="Kuala Belait">Kuala Belait</a>. After six days' fighting, they occupied the entire country. The only Allied troops in the area were the 2nd Battalion of the <a href="/wiki/15th_Punjab_Regiment" title="15th Punjab Regiment">15th Punjab Regiment</a> based at <a href="/wiki/Kuching" title="Kuching">Kuching</a>, Sarawak.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Once the Japanese occupied Brunei, they made an agreement with <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Tajuddin" title="Ahmad Tajuddin">Sultan Ahmad Tajuddin</a> over governing the country. Inche Ibrahim (known later as Pehin Datu Perdana Menteri Dato Laila Utama Awang Haji Ibrahim), a former Secretary to the British Resident, Ernest Edgar Pengilly, was appointed <a href="/wiki/Chief_Administrative_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Administrative Officer">Chief Administrative Officer</a> under the Japanese Governor. The Japanese had proposed that Pengilly retain his position under their administration, but he declined. Both he and other British nationals still in Brunei were interned by the Japanese at <a href="/wiki/Batu_Lintang_camp" title="Batu Lintang camp">Batu Lintang camp</a> in Sarawak. While the British officials were under Japanese guard, Ibrahim made a point of personally shaking each one by the hand and wishing him well.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Sultan retained his throne and was given a pension and honours by the Japanese. During the later part of the occupation, he resided at Tantuya, <a href="/wiki/Limbang" title="Limbang">Limbang</a> and had little to do with the Japanese. Most of the Malay government officers were retained by the Japanese. Brunei's administration was reorganised into five prefectures, which included British <a href="/wiki/North_Borneo" title="North Borneo">North Borneo</a>. The Prefectures included <a href="/wiki/Miri_Division" title="Miri Division">Baram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Labuan" title="Labuan">Labuan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lawas" title="Lawas">Lawas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Limbang" title="Limbang">Limbang</a>. Ibrahim hid numerous significant government documents from the Japanese during the occupation. Pengiran Yusuf (later YAM Pengiran Setia Negara Pengiran <a href="/wiki/Haji_Mohd_Yusuf" class="mw-redirect" title="Haji Mohd Yusuf">Haji Mohd Yusuf</a>), along with other Bruneians, was sent to Japan for training. Although in the area the day of the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">atomic bombing of Hiroshima</a>, Yusuf survived. </p>
      <p>The British had anticipated a Japanese attack, but lacked the resources to defend the area because of their engagement in the war in Europe. The troops from the Punjab Regiment filled in the <a href="/wiki/Seria" title="Seria">Seria</a> oilfield oilwells with concrete in September 1941 to deny the Japanese their use. The remaining equipment and installations were destroyed when the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Malaya" title="Japanese invasion of Malaya">Japanese invaded Malaya</a>. By the end of the war, 16 wells at <a href="/wiki/Miri,_Malaysia" class="mw-redirect" title="Miri, Malaysia">Miri</a> and Seria had been restarted, with production reaching about half the pre-war level. Coal production at <a href="/wiki/Muara,_Brunei" title="Muara, Brunei">Muara</a> was also recommenced, but with little success. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Japanese_battleships_at_Brunei,_Borneo,_in_October_1944_(NH_73090).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Japanese_battleships_at_Brunei%2C_Borneo%2C_in_October_1944_%28NH_73090%29.jpg/220px-Japanese_battleships_at_Brunei%2C_Borneo%2C_in_October_1944_%28NH_73090%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Japanese_battleships_at_Brunei%2C_Borneo%2C_in_October_1944_%28NH_73090%29.jpg/330px-Japanese_battleships_at_Brunei%2C_Borneo%2C_in_October_1944_%28NH_73090%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Japanese_battleships_at_Brunei%2C_Borneo%2C_in_October_1944_%28NH_73090%29.jpg/440px-Japanese_battleships_at_Brunei%2C_Borneo%2C_in_October_1944_%28NH_73090%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3629" data-file-height="2589"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Japanese_battleships_at_Brunei,_Borneo,_in_October_1944_(NH_73090).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Japanese_battleship_Nagato" title="Japanese battleship Nagato">IJN Nagato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_cruiser_Tone_(1937)" title="Japanese cruiser Tone (1937)">IJN Tone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_battleship_Yamato" title="Japanese battleship Yamato">IJN Yamato</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_battleship_Musashi" title="Japanese battleship Musashi">IJN Musashi</a> at Brunei in October 1944
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the occupation, the Japanese had their language taught in schools, and Government officers were required to learn Japanese. The local currency was replaced by what was to become known as <a href="/wiki/Banana_money" class="mw-redirect" title="Banana money"><i>duit pisang</i> (banana money)</a>. From 1943 hyper-inflation destroyed the currency's value and, at the end of the war, this currency was worthless. Allied attacks on shipping eventually caused trade to cease. Food and medicine fell into short supply, and the population suffered famine and disease. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Brunei_International_Airport" title="Brunei International Airport">airport</a> runway was constructed by the Japanese during the occupation, and in 1943 Japanese naval units were based in <a href="/wiki/Brunei_Bay" title="Brunei Bay">Brunei Bay</a> and Labuan. The naval base was destroyed by Allied bombing, but the airport runway survived. The facility was developed as a public airport. In 1944 the Allies began a bombing campaign against the occupying Japanese, which destroyed much of the town and Kuala Belait, but missed <a href="/wiki/Kampong_Ayer" title="Kampong Ayer">Kampong Ayer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Japanese_Surrender,_Labuan_(AWM_115989).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Japanese_Surrender%2C_Labuan_%28AWM_115989%29.JPG/220px-Japanese_Surrender%2C_Labuan_%28AWM_115989%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Japanese_Surrender%2C_Labuan_%28AWM_115989%29.JPG/330px-Japanese_Surrender%2C_Labuan_%28AWM_115989%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Japanese_Surrender%2C_Labuan_%28AWM_115989%29.JPG/440px-Japanese_Surrender%2C_Labuan_%28AWM_115989%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="632"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Japanese_Surrender,_Labuan_(AWM_115989).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/George_Wootten" title="George Wootten">Major-General Wootten</a> of the Australian 9th Division with <a href="/wiki/Masao_Baba" title="Masao Baba">Lieutenant-General Masao Baba</a> (signing) of the Japanese 37th Division at the surrender ceremony at Labuan on 10 September 1945
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 10 June 1945, the <a href="/wiki/Australian_9th_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian 9th Division">Australian 9th Division</a> landed at Muara under <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_North_Borneo" title="Battle of North Borneo">Operation Oboe Six</a> to recapture Borneo from the Japanese. They were supported by American air and naval units. Brunei town was bombed extensively and recaptured after three days of heavy fighting. Many buildings were destroyed, including the Mosque. The Japanese forces in Brunei, Borneo, and Sarawak, under Lieutenant-General Masao Baba, formally surrendered at Labuan on 10 September 1945. The British Military Administration took over from the Japanese and remained until July 1946. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-World_War_II">Post-World War II</span></h3> 
      <p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, a new government was formed in Brunei under the <a href="/wiki/British_Military_Administration_(Borneo)" title="British Military Administration (Borneo)">British Military Administration</a> (BMA). It consisted mainly of Australian officers and servicemen.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200979_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200979-56">[56]</a></sup> The administration of Brunei was passed to the Civil Administration on 6 July 1945. The Brunei State Council was also revived that year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200980_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200980-57">[57]</a></sup> The BMA was tasked to revive the Bruneian economy, which was extensively damaged by the Japanese during their occupation. They also had to put out the fires on the wells of Seria, which had been set by the Japanese prior to their defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200980_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200980-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Before 1941, the Governor of the Straits Settlements, based in Singapore, was responsible for the duties of British High Commissioner for Brunei, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sarawak" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Sarawak">Sarawak</a>, and <a href="/wiki/North_Borneo" title="North Borneo">North Borneo</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200981_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200981-58">[58]</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/British_High_Commissioner" class="mw-redirect" title="British High Commissioner">British High Commissioner</a> for Brunei was the Governor of Sarawak, Sir Charles Ardon Clarke. The Barisan Pemuda ("Youth Movement") (abbreviated as BARIP) was the first political party to be formed in Brunei, on 12 April 1946. The party intended to "preserve the sovereignty of the Sultan and the country, and to defend the rights of the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Malays" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic Malays">Malays</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-History131_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History131-59">[59]</a></sup> BARIP also contributed to the composition of the country's national anthem. The party was dissolved in 1948 due to inactivity. </p>
      <p>In 1959, a new constitution was written declaring Brunei a self-governing state, while its foreign affairs, security, and defence remained the responsibility of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> A small <a href="/wiki/Rebellion" title="Rebellion">rebellion</a> erupted against the monarchy in 1962, which was suppressed with help of the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Known as the <a href="/wiki/Brunei_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Brunei Revolt">Brunei Revolt</a>, it contributed to the failure to create the <a href="/wiki/North_Borneo_Federation" title="North Borneo Federation">North Borneo Federation</a>. The rebellion partially affected Brunei's decision to opt out of the Malaysian Federation.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brunei gained its independence from the United Kingdom on 1 January 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> The official National Day, which celebrates the country's independence, is held by tradition on 23 February.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_of_the_Constitution">Writing of the Constitution</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Omar_Ali_Saifuddien_III.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Omar_Ali_Saifuddien_III.jpg/220px-Omar_Ali_Saifuddien_III.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="276" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Omar_Ali_Saifuddien_III.jpg/330px-Omar_Ali_Saifuddien_III.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Omar_Ali_Saifuddien_III.jpg/440px-Omar_Ali_Saifuddien_III.jpg 2x" data-file-width="701" data-file-height="880"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Omar_Ali_Saifuddien_III.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sultan <a href="/wiki/Omar_Ali_Saifuddien_III" title="Omar Ali Saifuddien III">Omar Ali Saifuddien III</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In July 1953, Sultan <a href="/wiki/Omar_Ali_Saifuddien_III" title="Omar Ali Saifuddien III">Omar Ali Saifuddien III</a> formed a seven-member committee named <i>Tujuh Serangkai</i>, to find out the citizens' views regarding a written constitution for Brunei. In May 1954, the Sultan, Resident and High Commissioner met to discuss the findings of the committee. They agreed to authorise the drafting of a constitution. In March 1959 Sultan Omar Ali Saifuddien III led a delegation to London to discuss the proposed Constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200998_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200998-63">[63]</a></sup> The British delegation was led by Sir <a href="/wiki/Alan_Lennox-Boyd" class="mw-redirect" title="Alan Lennox-Boyd">Alan Lennox-Boyd</a>, Secretary of State for the Colonies. The British Government later accepted the draft constitution. </p>
      <p>On 29 September 1959, the Constitution Agreement was signed in <a href="/wiki/Bandar_Seri_Begawan" title="Bandar Seri Begawan">Brunei Town</a>. The agreement was signed by Sultan Omar Ali Saifuddien III and Sir Robert Scott, the Commissioner-General for Southeast Asia. It included the following provisions:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200959_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200959-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>The Sultan was made the Supreme Head of State.</li> 
       <li>Brunei was responsible for its internal administration.</li> 
       <li>The British Government was responsible for foreign and defence affairs only.</li> 
       <li>The post of Resident was abolished and replaced by a British High Commissioner.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Five councils were set up:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam2009100_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam2009100-64">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>The Executive Council</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council_of_Brunei" title="Legislative Council of Brunei">The Legislative Council of Brunei</a></li> 
       <li>The Privy Council</li> 
       <li>The Council of Succession</li> 
       <li>The State Religious Council</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_development_plans">National development plans</span></h3> 
      <p>A series of National Development Plans was initiated by the 28th Sultan of Brunei, <a href="/wiki/Omar_Ali_Saifuddien_III" title="Omar Ali Saifuddien III">Omar Ali Saifuddien III</a>. </p>
      <p>The first was introduced in 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200992_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200992-65">[65]</a></sup> A total sum of B$100 million was approved by the Brunei State Council for the plan. E.R. Bevington, from the Colonial Office in <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, was appointed to implement it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam2009129_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam2009129-66">[66]</a></sup> A $US14 million Gas Plant was built under the plan. In 1954, survey and exploration work were undertaken by the Brunei Shell Petroleum on both offshore and onshore fields. By 1956, production reached 114,700 <a href="/wiki/Barrels_per_day" class="mw-redirect" title="Barrels per day">bpd</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:THE_BRITISH_ARMY_IN_BRUNEI,_JANUARY_1963.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/THE_BRITISH_ARMY_IN_BRUNEI%2C_JANUARY_1963.jpg/220px-THE_BRITISH_ARMY_IN_BRUNEI%2C_JANUARY_1963.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/THE_BRITISH_ARMY_IN_BRUNEI%2C_JANUARY_1963.jpg/330px-THE_BRITISH_ARMY_IN_BRUNEI%2C_JANUARY_1963.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/THE_BRITISH_ARMY_IN_BRUNEI%2C_JANUARY_1963.jpg/440px-THE_BRITISH_ARMY_IN_BRUNEI%2C_JANUARY_1963.jpg 2x" data-file-width="795" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:THE_BRITISH_ARMY_IN_BRUNEI,_JANUARY_1963.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>British soldiers in the <a href="/wiki/British_protectorate" title="British protectorate">British protectorate</a> of Brunei on guard in the <a href="/wiki/Seria_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="Seria Field">Seria oilfield</a>, January 1963
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The plan also aided the development of public education. By 1958, expenditure on education totalled at $4 million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam2009129_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam2009129-66">[66]</a></sup> Communications were improved, as new roads were built and reconstruction at Berakas Airport was completed in 1954.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200921_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200921-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The second National Development Plan was launched in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200921_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200921-67">[67]</a></sup> A major oil and gas field was discovered in 1963, with this discovery, <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_natural_gas" title="Liquefied natural gas">liquefied natural gas</a> became important. Developments in the oil and gas sector have continued, and oil production has steadily increased since then.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200996_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200996-68">[68]</a></sup> The plan also promoted the production of meat and eggs for consumption by citizens. The fishing industry increased its output by 25% throughout the course of the plan. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Panamax_ports" title="List of Panamax ports">deepwater port</a> at <a href="/wiki/Muara,_Brunei" title="Muara, Brunei">Muara</a> was also constructed during this period. Power requirements were met, and studies were made to provide electricity to rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200996_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHistory_for_Brunei_Darussalam200996-68">[68]</a></sup> Efforts were made to eradicate <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, an endemic disease in the region, with the help of the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>. Malaria cases were reduced from 300 cases in 1953 to only 66 cases in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-History129_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History129-69">[69]</a></sup> The death rate was reduced from 20 per thousand in 1947 to 11.3 per thousand in 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-History129_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History129-69">[69]</a></sup> Infectious disease has been prevented by public sanitation and improvement of drainage, and the provision of piped pure water to the population.<sup id="cite_ref-History129_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History129-69">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span></h3> 
      <p>On 14 November 1971, Sultan <a href="/wiki/Hassanal_Bolkiah" title="Hassanal Bolkiah">Hassanal Bolkiah</a> left for London to discuss matters regarding the amendments to the 1959 constitution. A new agreement was signed on 23 November 1971 with the British representative being <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Royle,_Baron_Fanshawe_of_Richmond" title="Anthony Royle, Baron Fanshawe of Richmond">Anthony Royle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under this agreement, the following terms were agreed upon: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Brunei was granted full internal self-government</li> 
       <li>The UK would still be responsible for external affairs and defence.</li> 
       <li>Brunei and the UK agreed to share the responsibility for security and defence.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>This agreement also caused <a href="/wiki/British_Military_Garrison_Brunei" class="mw-redirect" title="British Military Garrison Brunei">Gurkha units</a> to be deployed in Brunei, where they remain up to this day. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_of_Brunei_with_Janin_Erih.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Sultan_of_Brunei_with_Janin_Erih.jpg/220px-Sultan_of_Brunei_with_Janin_Erih.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Sultan_of_Brunei_with_Janin_Erih.jpg/330px-Sultan_of_Brunei_with_Janin_Erih.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Sultan_of_Brunei_with_Janin_Erih.jpg/440px-Sultan_of_Brunei_with_Janin_Erih.jpg 2x" data-file-width="563" data-file-height="439"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_of_Brunei_with_Janin_Erih.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sultan <a href="/wiki/Hassanal_Bolkiah" title="Hassanal Bolkiah">Hassanal Bolkiah</a> (right) in 2004
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 7 January 1979, another treaty was signed between Brunei and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. It was signed with Lord Goronwy-Roberts being the representative of the UK. This agreement granted Brunei to take over international responsibilities as an independent nation. Britain agreed to assist Brunei in diplomatic matters.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In May 1983, it was announced by the UK that the date of independence of Brunei would be 1 January 1984.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>On 31 December 1983, a mass gathering was held on main mosques on all four of the districts of the country and at midnight, on 1 January 1984, the Proclamation of Independence was read by Sultan Hassanal Bolkiah. The sultan subsequently assumed the title "<a href="/wiki/Majesty" title="Majesty">His Majesty</a>", rather than the previous "<a href="/wiki/His_Royal_Highness" class="mw-redirect" title="His Royal Highness">His Royal Highness</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Brunei was <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">admitted to the United Nations</a> on 22 September 1984, becoming the organisation's 159th member.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span></h3> 
      <p>In October 2013, Sultan Hassanal Bolkiah announced his intention to impose <a href="/wiki/Penal_Code" class="mw-redirect" title="Penal Code">Penal Code</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Sharia_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharia law">Sharia law</a> on the country's Muslims, which make up roughly two thirds of the country's population.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> This would be implemented in three phases, culminating in 2016, and making Brunei the first and only country in East Asia to introduce Sharia law into its penal code.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The move attracted international criticism,<sup id="cite_ref-MSNBC_2014-05-07_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC_2014-05-07-76">[76]</a></sup> the United Nations expressing "deep concern".<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-27216798_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-27216798-77">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Brunei" title="Geography of Brunei">Geography of Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Brunei is a southeast Asian country consisting of two unconnected parts with a total area of 5,765 square kilometres (2,226&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) on the island of Borneo. It has 161 kilometres (100&nbsp;mi) of coastline next to the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>, and it shares a 381&nbsp;km (237&nbsp;mi) border with Malaysia. It has 500 square kilometres (193&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of territorial waters, and a 200-nautical-mile (370&nbsp;km; 230&nbsp;mi) <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>About 97% of the population lives in the larger western part (<a href="/wiki/Belait_District" title="Belait District">Belait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tutong_District" title="Tutong District">Tutong</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brunei_and_Muara" class="mw-redirect" title="Brunei and Muara">Brunei-Muara</a>), while only about 10,000 people live in the mountainous eastern part (<a href="/wiki/Temburong_District" title="Temburong District">Temburong District</a>). The total population of Brunei is approximately 408,000 as of July 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brunei&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, of which around 150,000 live in the capital <a href="/wiki/Bandar_Seri_Begawan" title="Bandar Seri Begawan">Bandar Seri Begawan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Other major towns are the port town of <a href="/wiki/Muara,_Brunei" title="Muara, Brunei">Muara</a>, the oil-producing town of <a href="/wiki/Seria" title="Seria">Seria</a> and its neighbouring town, <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Belait" title="Kuala Belait">Kuala Belait</a>. In Belait District, the <a href="/wiki/Panaga" title="Panaga">Panaga</a> area is home to large numbers of Europeans expatriates, due to <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a> and British Army housing, and several recreational facilities are located there.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most of Brunei is within the <a href="/wiki/Borneo_lowland_rain_forests" title="Borneo lowland rain forests">Borneo lowland rain forests</a> ecoregion, which covers most of the island. Areas of <a href="/wiki/Borneo_montane_rain_forests" title="Borneo montane rain forests">mountain rain forests</a> are located inland.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_Bandar_Seri_Begawan_19.05.2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Panorama_Bandar_Seri_Begawan_19.05.2018.jpg/800px-Panorama_Bandar_Seri_Begawan_19.05.2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="450" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Panorama_Bandar_Seri_Begawan_19.05.2018.jpg/1200px-Panorama_Bandar_Seri_Begawan_19.05.2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Panorama_Bandar_Seri_Begawan_19.05.2018.jpg/1600px-Panorama_Bandar_Seri_Begawan_19.05.2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2967" data-file-height="1668"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_Bandar_Seri_Begawan_19.05.2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div>A panorama of <a href="/wiki/Bandar_Seri_Begawan" title="Bandar Seri Begawan">Bandar Seri Begawan</a>, capital and largest city of Brunei.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Brunei" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Brunei">climate of Brunei</a> is <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a> equatorial that is a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">Tropical rainforest climate</a><sup id="cite_ref-cia_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-26">[26]</a></sup> more subject to the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a> than the <a href="/wiki/Trade_wind" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade wind">trade winds</a> and with no or rare <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">cyclones</a>. Brunei is exposed to the risks stemming from climate change along with other ASEAN member states.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Brunei" title="Politics of Brunei">Politics of Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hassanal_Bolkiah.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Hassanal_Bolkiah.jpg/170px-Hassanal_Bolkiah.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Hassanal_Bolkiah.jpg/255px-Hassanal_Bolkiah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/53/Hassanal_Bolkiah.jpg 2x" data-file-width="312" data-file-height="416"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hassanal_Bolkiah.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Hassanal_Bolkiah" title="Hassanal Bolkiah">Hassanal Bolkiah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sultan_of_Brunei" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultan of Brunei">Sultan of Brunei</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Brunei's political system is governed by the constitution and the national tradition of the Malay Islamic Monarchy (<i><a href="/wiki/Melayu_Islam_Beraja" title="Melayu Islam Beraja">Melayu Islam Beraja</a></i>; MIB). The three components of MIB cover Malay culture, Islamic religion, and the political framework under the monarchy.<sup id="cite_ref-bruneipress.com.bn_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bruneipress.com.bn-82">[82]</a></sup> It has a legal system based on <a href="/wiki/English_common_law" class="mw-redirect" title="English common law">English common law</a>, although Islamic law (<i><a href="/wiki/Shariah" class="mw-redirect" title="Shariah">shariah</a></i>) supersedes this in some cases.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-26">[26]</a></sup> Brunei <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council_of_Brunei" title="Legislative Council of Brunei">has a parliament</a> but there are no elections; the last election was held in <a href="/wiki/Brunei_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Brunei Revolt">1962</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under Brunei's 1959 constitution, <a href="/wiki/His_Majesty_Paduka_Seri_Baginda_Sultan_Haji_Hassanal_Bolkiah_Mu%27izzaddin_Waddaulah" class="mw-redirect" title="His Majesty Paduka Seri Baginda Sultan Haji Hassanal Bolkiah Mu'izzaddin Waddaulah">His Majesty Paduka Seri Baginda Sultan Haji Hassanal Bolkiah Mu'izzaddin Waddaulah</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> with full executive authority. Since <a href="/wiki/Brunei_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Brunei Revolt">1962</a>, this authority has included emergency powers, which are renewed every two years. Brunei has technically been under <a href="/wiki/Martial_law" title="Martial law">martial law</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Brunei_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Brunei Revolt">Brunei Revolt</a> of 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hassanal_Bolkiah" title="Hassanal Bolkiah">Hassanal Bolkiah</a> also serves as the state's Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Finance_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Finance Minister">Finance Minister</a> and <a href="/wiki/Defence_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Defence Minister">Defence Minister</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The Royal family retains a venerated status within Brunei.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (April 2015)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Brunei" title="Foreign relations of Brunei">Foreign relations of Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pres._Obama_and_HM_Bolkiah_APEC_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pres._Obama_and_HM_Bolkiah_APEC_2015.jpg/220px-Pres._Obama_and_HM_Bolkiah_APEC_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pres._Obama_and_HM_Bolkiah_APEC_2015.jpg/330px-Pres._Obama_and_HM_Bolkiah_APEC_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pres._Obama_and_HM_Bolkiah_APEC_2015.jpg/440px-Pres._Obama_and_HM_Bolkiah_APEC_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="654" data-file-height="436"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pres._Obama_and_HM_Bolkiah_APEC_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Brunei's Sultan and Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Hassanal_Bolkiah" title="Hassanal Bolkiah">Hassanal Bolkiah</a> meets with U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, 18 November 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Keroncong_Kemayoran_di_Perayaan_50_Tahun_Sultan_Hassanal_Bolkiah_Bertakhta_(2c).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Keroncong_Kemayoran_di_Perayaan_50_Tahun_Sultan_Hassanal_Bolkiah_Bertakhta_%282c%29.jpg/220px-Keroncong_Kemayoran_di_Perayaan_50_Tahun_Sultan_Hassanal_Bolkiah_Bertakhta_%282c%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Keroncong_Kemayoran_di_Perayaan_50_Tahun_Sultan_Hassanal_Bolkiah_Bertakhta_%282c%29.jpg/330px-Keroncong_Kemayoran_di_Perayaan_50_Tahun_Sultan_Hassanal_Bolkiah_Bertakhta_%282c%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Keroncong_Kemayoran_di_Perayaan_50_Tahun_Sultan_Hassanal_Bolkiah_Bertakhta_%282c%29.jpg/440px-Keroncong_Kemayoran_di_Perayaan_50_Tahun_Sultan_Hassanal_Bolkiah_Bertakhta_%282c%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="832" data-file-height="624"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Keroncong_Kemayoran_di_Perayaan_50_Tahun_Sultan_Hassanal_Bolkiah_Bertakhta_(2c).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sultan Hassanal Bolkiah with Indonesian President <a href="/wiki/Joko_Widodo" title="Joko Widodo">Joko Widodo</a>, 6 October 2017
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Until 1979, Brunei's foreign relations were managed by the UK government. After that, they were handled by the Brunei Diplomatic Service. After independence in 1984, this Service was upgraded to ministerial level and is now known as the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Officially, Brunei's foreign policy is as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Mutual respect of others' territorial sovereignty, integrity and independence;</li> 
       <li>The maintenance of friendly relations among nations;</li> 
       <li>Non-interference in the internal affairs of other countries; and</li> 
       <li>The maintenance and the promotion of peace, security and stability in the region.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>With its traditional ties with the United Kingdom, Brunei became the 49th member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> immediately on the day of its independence on 1 January 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> As one of its first initiatives toward improved regional relations, Brunei joined <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a> on 7 January 1984, becoming the sixth member. To achieve recognition of its sovereignty and independence, it joined the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> as a full member on 21 September of that same year.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As an Islamic country, Brunei became a full member of the Organisation of the Islamic Conference (now the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>) in January 1984 at the Fourth Islamic Summit held in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After its accession to the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation</a> forum (APEC) in 1989, Brunei hosted the APEC Economic Leaders' Meeting in November 2000 and the ASEAN Regional Forum (ARF) in July 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-APEC_2000_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APEC_2000-90">[90]</a></sup> Brunei became a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO) on 1 January 1995,<sup id="cite_ref-WTO_2008_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WTO_2008-91">[91]</a></sup> and is a major player in <a href="/wiki/BIMP-EAGA" title="BIMP-EAGA">BIMP-EAGA</a>, which was formed during the Inaugural Ministers' Meeting in <a href="/wiki/Davao_City" title="Davao City">Davao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, on 24 March 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-BIMP_1994_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BIMP_1994-92">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brunei shares a close relationship with <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> and the Philippines. In April 2009, Brunei and the Philippines signed a <a href="/wiki/Memorandum_of_Understanding" class="mw-redirect" title="Memorandum of Understanding">Memorandum of Understanding</a> (MOU) that seeks to strengthen the bilateral co-operation of the two countries in the fields of agriculture and farm-related trade and investments.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brunei is one of many nations to lay claim to some of the disputed <a href="/wiki/Spratly_Islands" title="Spratly Islands">Spratly Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dispute_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dispute-94">[94]</a></sup> The status of <a href="/wiki/Limbang" title="Limbang">Limbang</a> as part of Sarawak has been disputed by Brunei since the area was first annexed in 1890.<sup id="cite_ref-dispute_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dispute-94">[94]</a></sup> The issue was reportedly settled in 2009, with Brunei agreeing to accept the border in exchange for Malaysia giving up claims to oil fields in Bruneian waters.<sup id="cite_ref-bt_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-95">[95]</a></sup> The Brunei government denies this and says that their claim on Limbang was never dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brunei was the chair for <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> It also hosted the ASEAN summit on that same year.<sup id="cite_ref-RA_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RA-99">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Defence">Defence</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Brunei_Armed_Forces" title="Royal Brunei Armed Forces">Royal Brunei Armed Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Military_Garrison_Brunei" class="mw-redirect" title="British Military Garrison Brunei">British Military Garrison Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Brunei maintains three infantry battalions stationed around the country.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Brunei_Navy" title="Royal Brunei Navy">Brunei navy</a> has several "Ijtihad"-class patrol boats purchased from a German manufacturer. The United Kingdom also maintains a base in <a href="/wiki/Seria" title="Seria">Seria</a>, the centre of the oil industry in Brunei. A <a href="/wiki/Gurkha" title="Gurkha">Gurkha</a> battalion consisting of 1,500 personnel is stationed there.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> United Kingdom military personnel are stationed there under a defence agreement signed between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/Bell_212" title="Bell 212">Bell 212</a> operated by the air force crashed in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Belait" title="Kuala Belait">Kuala Belait</a> on 20 July 2012 with the loss of 12 of the 14 crew on board. The cause of the accident has yet to be ascertained.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The crash is the worst aviation incident in the history of Brunei. </p>
      <p>The Army is currently acquiring new equipment,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/UAV" class="mw-redirect" title="UAV">UAVs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sikorsky_S-70" title="Sikorsky S-70">S-70i Black Hawks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brunei's Legislative Council proposed an increase of the defence budget for the 2016–17 fiscal year of about five percent to 564 million Brunei dollars ($408 million). This amounts to about ten per cent of the state's total national yearly expenditure and represents around 2.5 per cent of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Brunei" title="Districts of Brunei">Districts of Brunei</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mukims_of_Brunei" title="Mukims of Brunei">Mukims of Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Brunei is divided into four districts (<i><a href="/wiki/Daerah" class="mw-redirect" title="Daerah">daerahs</a></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> and 38 subdistricts (<i><a href="/wiki/Mukim" title="Mukim">mukims</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The daerah of Temburong is physically separated from the rest of Brunei by the <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysian</a> state of <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a>. </p>

        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#fdb395; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Brunei-Muara_District" title="Brunei-Muara District">Brunei-Muara</a>
        </div>
       </div> 
       <div style="position:absolute; left:34px; top:116px">
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
        <div class="legend">

        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The daerah of Brunei-Muara includes Brunei's capital city, <a href="/wiki/Bandar_Seri_Begawan" title="Bandar Seri Begawan">Bandar Seri Begawan</a>, whose suburbs dominate 15 of the 18 mukims in this daerah. </p>
      <p>Over 90% of Brunei's total population lives in 15 of the 38 mukims: </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">Legal system</span></h2> 
      <p>Brunei has numerous courts in its judicial branch. The highest court is the Supreme Court, which consists of the Court of Appeal and High Court. Both of these have a chief justice and two judges.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_26-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-26">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women_and_children">Women and children</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Brunei" title="Women in Brunei">Women in Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_111004-N-VP123-071_Lt._j.g._Artemas_Richardson,_a_public_affairs_officer_aboard_the_Arleigh_Burke-class_guided-missile_destroyer_USS_Dewey.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/US_Navy_111004-N-VP123-071_Lt._j.g._Artemas_Richardson%2C_a_public_affairs_officer_aboard_the_Arleigh_Burke-class_guided-missile_destroyer_USS_Dewey.jpg/220px-US_Navy_111004-N-VP123-071_Lt._j.g._Artemas_Richardson%2C_a_public_affairs_officer_aboard_the_Arleigh_Burke-class_guided-missile_destroyer_USS_Dewey.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/US_Navy_111004-N-VP123-071_Lt._j.g._Artemas_Richardson%2C_a_public_affairs_officer_aboard_the_Arleigh_Burke-class_guided-missile_destroyer_USS_Dewey.jpg/330px-US_Navy_111004-N-VP123-071_Lt._j.g._Artemas_Richardson%2C_a_public_affairs_officer_aboard_the_Arleigh_Burke-class_guided-missile_destroyer_USS_Dewey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/US_Navy_111004-N-VP123-071_Lt._j.g._Artemas_Richardson%2C_a_public_affairs_officer_aboard_the_Arleigh_Burke-class_guided-missile_destroyer_USS_Dewey.jpg/440px-US_Navy_111004-N-VP123-071_Lt._j.g._Artemas_Richardson%2C_a_public_affairs_officer_aboard_the_Arleigh_Burke-class_guided-missile_destroyer_USS_Dewey.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_111004-N-VP123-071_Lt._j.g._Artemas_Richardson,_a_public_affairs_officer_aboard_the_Arleigh_Burke-class_guided-missile_destroyer_USS_Dewey.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Headscarves called <i><a href="/wiki/Tudong" title="Tudong">tudong</a></i> are compulsory for Brunei's Muslim schoolgirls
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The U.S. Department of State has stated that discrimination against women is a problem in Brunei.<sup id="cite_ref-state.gov_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state.gov-106">[106]</a></sup> The law prohibits sexual harassment and stipulates that whoever assaults or uses criminal force, intending thereby to outrage or knowing it is likely to outrage the modesty of a person, shall be punished with imprisonment for as much as five years and <a href="/wiki/Caning" title="Caning">caning</a>. The law stipulates imprisonment of up to 30 years, and caning with not fewer than 12 strokes for rape. The law does not criminalise spousal rape; it explicitly states that sexual intercourse by a man with his wife, as long as she is not under 13 years of age, is not rape. Protections against sexual assault by a spouse are provided under the amended Islamic Family Law Order 2010 and Married Women Act Order 2010. The penalty for breaching a protection order is a fine not exceeding BN$2,000 ($1,538) or imprisonment not exceeding six months. </p>
      <p>Citizenship is derived through one's parents rather than through birth within the country's territory. Parents with stateless status are required to apply for a special pass for a child born in the country; failure to register a child may make it difficult to enroll the child in school. By law, sexual intercourse with a female under 14 years of age constitutes rape and is punishable by imprisonment for not less than eight years and not more than 30 years and not less than 12 strokes of the cane. The intent of the law is to protect girls from exploitation through prostitution and "other immoral purposes", including pornography.<sup id="cite_ref-state.gov_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state.gov-106">[106]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_rights">LGBT rights</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Brunei" title="Freedom of religion in Brunei">Freedom of religion in Brunei</a> and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Brunei" title="LGBT rights in Brunei">LGBT rights in Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Male and female <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> is <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Brunei" title="LGBT rights in Brunei">illegal in Brunei</a>. Sexual relations between men are punishable by death or whipping; sex between women is punishable by caning or imprisonment. </p>
      <p>In May 2019, the Brunei government extended its existing moratorium on the death penalty to the Sharia criminal code as well that made homosexual acts punishable with death by stoning.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_rights">Religious rights</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Brunei_International_Airport_Surau.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Brunei_International_Airport_Surau.jpg/220px-Brunei_International_Airport_Surau.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Brunei_International_Airport_Surau.jpg/330px-Brunei_International_Airport_Surau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Brunei_International_Airport_Surau.jpg/440px-Brunei_International_Airport_Surau.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4128" data-file-height="3096"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Brunei_International_Airport_Surau.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Brunei International Airport Mosque
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In The Laws of Brunei, the right of non-Muslims to practice their faith is guaranteed by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brunei" title="Constitution of Brunei">1959 Constitution</a>. However, celebrations and prayers must be confined to places of worship and private residences.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Upon adopting Sharia Penal Code, the Ministry of Religious Affairs banned <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> decorations in public places, but did not forbid celebration of Christmas in places of worship and private premises.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The international media reports of a “Christmas ban” which spread in 2014 in Brunei were exaggerated, failing to mention that celebrations continue within churches and among the different Christian communities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On 25 December 2015, 4,000 out of 18,000 estimated local Catholics attended the mass of Christmas Day and Christmas Eve.<sup id="cite_ref-m.bt.com.bn_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-m.bt.com.bn-109">[109]</a></sup> In 2015, the head of the Catholic Church in Brunei told <a href="/wiki/The_Brunei_Times" title="The Brunei Times">The Brunei Times</a>, "To be quite honest there has been no change for us this year; no new restrictions have been laid down, although we fully respect and adhere to the existing regulations that our celebrations and worship be [confined] to the compounds of the church and private residences".<sup id="cite_ref-m.bt.com.bn_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-m.bt.com.bn-109">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brunei's revised penal code came into force in phases, commencing on 22 April 2014 with offences punishable by fines or imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-Brunei140430_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brunei140430-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DW-140430_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DW-140430-111">[111]</a></sup> The complete code, due for final implementation later, stipulated the <a href="/wiki/Death_penalty" class="mw-redirect" title="Death penalty">death penalty</a> for numerous offenses (both violent and non-violent), such as insult or defamation of <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>, insulting any verses of the Quran and Hadith, <a href="/wiki/Blasphemy" title="Blasphemy">blasphemy</a>, declaring oneself a prophet or non-Muslim, robbery, rape, adultery, sodomy, extramarital sexual relations for Muslims, and murder. Stoning to death was the specified "method of execution for crimes of a sexual nature". Rupert Colville, spokesperson for the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_UN_High_Commissioner_for_Human_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of the UN High Commissioner for Human Rights">Office of the UN High Commissioner for Human Rights</a> (OHCHR) declared that, "Application of the death penalty for such a broad range of offences contravenes international law."<sup id="cite_ref-UN_2014_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_2014-112">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Animal_rights">Animal rights</span></h3> 
      <p>Brunei is the first country in Asia to have banned <a href="/wiki/Shark_finning" title="Shark finning">shark finning</a> nationwide.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brunei has retained most of its forests, compared to its neighbours that share <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a> island. There is a public campaign calling to protect <a href="/wiki/Pangolin" title="Pangolin">pangolins</a> which are considered threatened treasure in Brunei.<sup id="cite_ref-Hii2015_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hii2015-114">[114]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Brunei" title="Economy of Brunei">Economy of Brunei</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Brunei" title="Tourism in Brunei">Tourism in Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Brunei_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Brunei_Export_Treemap.jpg/220px-Brunei_Export_Treemap.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Brunei_Export_Treemap.jpg/330px-Brunei_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Brunei_Export_Treemap.jpg/440px-Brunei_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1104" data-file-height="863"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Brunei_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Brunei's product exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SBY_dan_para_pemimpin_ASEAN_25-04-2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/SBY_dan_para_pemimpin_ASEAN_25-04-2013.jpg/220px-SBY_dan_para_pemimpin_ASEAN_25-04-2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/SBY_dan_para_pemimpin_ASEAN_25-04-2013.jpg/330px-SBY_dan_para_pemimpin_ASEAN_25-04-2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/SBY_dan_para_pemimpin_ASEAN_25-04-2013.jpg/440px-SBY_dan_para_pemimpin_ASEAN_25-04-2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1144"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SBY_dan_para_pemimpin_ASEAN_25-04-2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/BIMP-EAGA" title="BIMP-EAGA">BIMP-EAGA</a> meeting in the office of Brunei Prime Minister on 25 April 2013. From left: Brunei Sultan Hassanal Bolkiah, Indonesian President <a href="/wiki/Susilo_Bambang_Yudhoyono" title="Susilo Bambang Yudhoyono">Susilo Bambang Yudhoyono</a>, Malaysian Representative and Filipino President <a href="/wiki/Benigno_Aquino_III" title="Benigno Aquino III">Benigno Aquino III</a>. Brunei is part of the BIMP-EAGA, a subregional economic co-operation initiative in Southeast Asia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Brunei has the second-highest <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> among the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeast Asian">Southeast Asian</a> nations, after <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, and is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Crude oil</a> and natural gas production account for about 90% of its GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> About 167,000 barrels (26,600&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>) of oil are produced every day, making Brunei the fourth-largest producer of oil in Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> It also produces approximately 25.3&nbsp;million cubic metres (890<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&nbsp;cu&nbsp;ft) of <a href="/wiki/Liquified_natural_gas" class="mw-redirect" title="Liquified natural gas">liquified natural gas</a> per day, making Brunei the ninth-largest gas exporter in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> also ranks Brunei as the fifth-richest nation out of 182, based on its petroleum and natural gas fields.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Substantial income from overseas investment supplements income from domestic production. Most of these investments are made by the Brunei Investment Agency, an arm of the Ministry of Finance.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> The government provides for all medical services,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> and subsidises rice<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> and housing.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The national <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">air carrier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Brunei_Airlines" title="Royal Brunei Airlines">Royal Brunei Airlines</a>, is trying to develop Brunei as a hub for international travel between Europe and Australia/New Zealand. Central to this strategy is the position that the airline maintains at London Heathrow Airport. It holds a daily slot at the highly capacity-controlled airport, which it serves from Bandar Seri Begawan via Dubai. The airline also has services to major Asian destinations including Shanghai, Bangkok, Singapore and Manila. </p>
      <p>Brunei depends heavily on imports such as agricultural products (e.g. rice, <a href="/wiki/Convenience_food" title="Convenience food">food products</a>, livestock, etc.),<sup id="cite_ref-agriculture_brunei_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agriculture_brunei-119">[119]</a></sup>vehicles and <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">electrical products</a> from other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Brunei imports 60% of its food; of that amount, around 75% come from other ASEAN countries.<sup id="cite_ref-agriculture_brunei_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agriculture_brunei-119">[119]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brunei's leaders are concerned that increasing integration in the world economy will undermine internal <a href="/wiki/Social_cohesion" class="mw-redirect" title="Social cohesion">social cohesion</a> and have therefore pursued an isolationist policy. However, it has become a more prominent player by serving as chairman for the 2000 <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation</a> (APEC) forum. Brunei's leaders plan to upgrade the <a href="/wiki/Labour_(economics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour (economics)">labour</a> force, reduce unemployment, which was at 6.9% in 2014;<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> strengthen the banking and tourism sectors, and, in general, broaden the economic base.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> A long-term development plan aims to diversify growth.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government of Brunei has also promoted food self-sufficiency, especially in <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>. Brunei renamed its Brunei Darussalam Rice 1 as Laila Rice during the launch of the "Padi Planting Towards Achieving Self-Sufficiency of Rice Production in Brunei Darussalam" ceremony at the Wasan padi fields in April 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In August 2009, the Royal Family reaped the first few Laila padi stalks, after years of attempts to boost local rice production, a goal first articulated about half a century ago.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> In July 2009 Brunei launched its national <a href="/wiki/Halal" title="Halal">halal</a> branding scheme, Brunei Halal, with a goal to export to foreign markets.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:V8-DLA_Boeing_787_of_Royal_Brunei_at_Heathrow_(11400528073).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/V8-DLA_Boeing_787_of_Royal_Brunei_at_Heathrow_%2811400528073%29.jpg/220px-V8-DLA_Boeing_787_of_Royal_Brunei_at_Heathrow_%2811400528073%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/V8-DLA_Boeing_787_of_Royal_Brunei_at_Heathrow_%2811400528073%29.jpg/330px-V8-DLA_Boeing_787_of_Royal_Brunei_at_Heathrow_%2811400528073%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/V8-DLA_Boeing_787_of_Royal_Brunei_at_Heathrow_%2811400528073%29.jpg/440px-V8-DLA_Boeing_787_of_Royal_Brunei_at_Heathrow_%2811400528073%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2101" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:V8-DLA_Boeing_787_of_Royal_Brunei_at_Heathrow_(11400528073).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Royal Brunei <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787 Dreamliner</a> at London <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport_Holdings" title="Heathrow Airport Holdings">Heathrow Airport</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The population centres in the country are linked by a network of 2,800 kilometres (1,700&nbsp;mi) of road. The 135-kilometre (84&nbsp;mi) highway from Muara Town to Kuala Belait is a <a href="/wiki/Dual_carriageway" title="Dual carriageway">dual carriageway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bruneipress.com.bn_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bruneipress.com.bn-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brunei is accessible by air, sea, and land transport. <a href="/wiki/Brunei_International_Airport" title="Brunei International Airport">Brunei International Airport</a> is the main entry point to the country. <a href="/wiki/Royal_Brunei_Airlines" title="Royal Brunei Airlines">Royal Brunei Airlines</a><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> is the national carrier. There is another airfield, the <a href="/wiki/Anduki_Airfield" title="Anduki Airfield">Anduki Airfield</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Seria" title="Seria">Seria</a>. The ferry terminal at Muara services regular connections to <a href="/wiki/Labuan" title="Labuan">Labuan</a> (Malaysia). Speedboats provide passenger and goods transportation to the Temburong district.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The main highway running across Brunei is the Tutong-Muara Highway. The country's road network is well developed. Brunei has one main sea port located at Muara.<sup id="cite_ref-US_DOS_60-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_DOS-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The airport in Brunei is currently being extensively upgraded.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Changi Airport International is the consultant working on this modernisation, which planned cost is currently $150 million.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_null_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_null-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aviation_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aviation-131">[131]</a></sup> This project is slated to add 14,000 square metres (150,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;ft) of new floorspace and includes a new terminal and arrival hall.<sup id="cite_ref-BT22_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT22-132">[132]</a></sup> With the completion of this project, the annual passenger capacity of the airport is expected to double from 1.5 to 3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_null_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_null-130">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With one private car for every 2.09 persons, Brunei has one of the highest car ownership rates in the world. This has been attributed to the absence of a comprehensive transport system, low import tax, and low unleaded petrol price of B$0.53 per litre.<sup id="cite_ref-bruneipress.com.bn_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bruneipress.com.bn-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A new 30-kilometre (19&nbsp;mi) roadway <a href="/wiki/Temburong_Bridge" title="Temburong Bridge">connecting the Muara and Temburong</a> districts of Brunei is slated to be completed in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Fourteen kilometres (9&nbsp;mi) of this roadway would be crossing the <a href="/wiki/Brunei_Bay" title="Brunei Bay">Brunei Bay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> The bridge cost is $1.6 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Banking">Banking</span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_China" title="Bank of China">Bank of China</a> received permission to open a branch in Brunei in April 2016. <a href="/wiki/Citibank" title="Citibank">Citibank</a>, which entered in 1972, closed its operations in Brunei in 2014. <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a>, which had entered in 1947, closed its operation in Brunei in November 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-HSBCClose_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSBCClose-136">[136]</a></sup> May Bank of Malaysia, RHB Bank of Malaysia, Standard Chartered Bank of United Kingdom, United Overseas Bank of Singapore and Bank of China are currently operating in Brunei. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Brunei" title="Demographics of Brunei">Demographics of Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_Omar_Ali_Saifuddin_Mosque_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Sultan_Omar_Ali_Saifuddin_Mosque_02.jpg/220px-Sultan_Omar_Ali_Saifuddin_Mosque_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Sultan_Omar_Ali_Saifuddin_Mosque_02.jpg/330px-Sultan_Omar_Ali_Saifuddin_Mosque_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Sultan_Omar_Ali_Saifuddin_Mosque_02.jpg/440px-Sultan_Omar_Ali_Saifuddin_Mosque_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3933" data-file-height="2622"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_Omar_Ali_Saifuddin_Mosque_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sultan_Omar_Ali_Saifuddin_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultan Omar Ali Saifuddin Mosque">Sultan Omar Ali Saifuddin Mosque</a> at night.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
