      <p>Ethnicities indigenous to Brunei include the <a href="/wiki/Belait_people" title="Belait people">Belait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei_Bisaya_language" title="Brunei Bisaya language">Brunei Bisaya</a> (not to be confused with the Bisaya/Visaya of the nearby Philippines), indigenous <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Malay_people" title="Bruneian Malay people">Bruneian Malay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dusun_people" title="Dusun people">Dusun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kedayan" title="Kedayan">Kedayan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lun_Bawang" title="Lun Bawang">Lun Bawang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murut_people" title="Murut people">Murut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tutong_language" title="Tutong language">Tutong</a>. </p>
      <p>The population of Brunei in 2018 was 428,963,<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-137">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-138">[138]</a></sup> of which 76% live in urban areas. The rate of urbanisation is estimated at 2.13% per year from 2010 to 2015. The average life expectancy is 77.7 years.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> In 2014, 65.7% of the population were <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Malay_people" title="Bruneian Malay people">Malay</a>, 10.3% are <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Chinese_in_Brunei" title="Ethnic Chinese in Brunei">Chinese</a>, 3.4% are indigenous, with 20.6% smaller groups making up the rest.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> There is a relatively large <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriate</a> community.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> Most expats come from non-<a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> countries such as Australia, United Kingdom, South Korea, Japan, The Philippines, Thailand, Cambodia, Vietnam and India. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Brunei" title="Religion in Brunei">Religion in Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black"> 
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:grey"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 137.63819204712px; border-left-color:blue"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:blue"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:blue"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 32.491969623291px; border-left-color:orange"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:orange"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:orange"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:87.630668004386px 48.175367410172px 0 0; border-top-color:green"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:green"></div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Religion in Brunei </p> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:green; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> 296,408 (67%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:orange; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> 57,512 (13%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:blue; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> 44,240 (10%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:grey; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;indigenous beliefs and non-religious, Atheist or <a href="/wiki/Agnostic" class="mw-redirect" title="Agnostic">Agnostic</a> 44,240 (10%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Brunei" title="Islam in Brunei">Islam</a> is the official religion of Brunei,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_26-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-26">[26]</a></sup> specifically that of the <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> denomination and the <a href="/wiki/Shafi%E2%80%98i" class="mw-redirect" title="Shafi‘i">Shafi‘i</a> school of Islamic jurisprudence. Two-thirds of the population, including the majority of <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Malay_people" title="Bruneian Malay people">Bruneian Malays</a> identify as <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>. Other faiths practised are <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Brunei" title="Buddhism in Brunei">Buddhism</a> (13%, mainly by the Chinese) and <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Brunei" title="Christianity in Brunei">Christianity</a> (10%).<sup id="cite_ref-cia_26-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Freethought" class="mw-redirect" title="Freethought">Freethinkers</a>, mostly Chinese, form about 7% of the population. Although most of them practise some form of religion with elements of Buddhism, <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a>, they prefer to present themselves as having practised no religion officially, hence labelled as <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheists</a> in official censuses. Followers of indigenous religions are about 2% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Brunei" title="Languages of Brunei">Languages of Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The official <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Brunei" title="Languages of Brunei">language of Brunei</a> is <a href="/wiki/Standard_Malay" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Malay">Standard Malay</a>, for which both the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rumi_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Rumi script">Rumi</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Arabic_alphabet" title="Arabic alphabet">Arabic alphabet</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jawi_alphabet" title="Jawi alphabet">Jawi</a>) are used.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Initially, the usage script to write Malay words are conducted in Jawi alphabet before it was switched in to Latin alphabet around 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEde_Vienne2016104_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_Vienne2016104-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The principal spoken language is <i>Melayu Brunei</i> (<a href="/wiki/Brunei_Malay" title="Brunei Malay">Brunei Malay</a>). Brunei Malay is rather divergent from standard Malay and the rest of the Malay dialects, being about 84% cognate with standard Malay,<sup id="cite_ref-Martin_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martin-145">[145]</a></sup> and is mostly mutually unintelligible with it.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is widely used as a business and official language and it is spoken by a majority of the population in Brunei. English is used in business as a <a href="/wiki/Working_language" title="Working language">working language</a> and as the language of instruction from primary to tertiary education.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Chinese languages are also widely spoken, and the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Chinese_in_Brunei" title="Ethnic Chinese in Brunei">Chinese minority</a> in Brunei speak a number of <a href="/wiki/Varieties_of_Chinese" title="Varieties of Chinese">varieties of Chinese</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> is the religious language of Muslims. Therefore, Arabic is taught in schools, particularly religious schools, and also in institutes of higher learning. As of 2004, there are six Arabic schools and one religious teachers' college in Brunei. A majority of Brunei's Muslim population has had some form of formal or informal education in the reading, writing and pronunciation of the Arabic language as part of their religious education. </p>
      <p>Other languages and dialects spoken include <a href="/wiki/Kedayan_Malay" class="mw-redirect" title="Kedayan Malay">Kedayan Malay</a> dialect, <a href="/wiki/Tutong_language" title="Tutong language">Tutong Malay dialect</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murutic_languages" title="Murutic languages">Murut</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dusun_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dusun language">Dusun</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Martin_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martin-145">[145]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Brunei" title="Culture of Brunei">Culture of Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Regalie_(1).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Royal_Regalie_%281%29.JPG/220px-Royal_Regalie_%281%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Royal_Regalie_%281%29.JPG/330px-Royal_Regalie_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Royal_Regalie_%281%29.JPG/440px-Royal_Regalie_%281%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3216" data-file-height="2461"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Regalie_(1).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Royal Regalia Museum
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The culture of Brunei is predominantly <a href="/wiki/Malay_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Malay people">Malay</a> (reflecting its ethnicity), with heavy influences from <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, but is seen as much more conservative than <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> Influences to Bruneian culture come from the Malay cultures of the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Archipelago" title="Malay Archipelago">Malay Archipelago</a>. Four periods of cultural influence have occurred, animist, <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a>, Islamic, and Western. Islam had a very strong influence, and was adopted as Brunei's ideology and philosophy. Brunei's official main language is <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> but English is also widely spoken as it is a compulsory subject in the majority of the schools.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia</a> country, the sale and public consumption of alcohol is banned.<sup id="cite_ref-Brunei_Tourism_Website_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brunei_Tourism_Website-153">[153]</a></sup> Non-Muslims are allowed to bring in a limited amount of alcohol from their point of embarkation overseas for their own private consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-bruneipress.com.bn_82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bruneipress.com.bn-82">[82]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Brunei" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Brunei">Media of Brunei</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Media in Brunei are said to be pro-government; press criticism of the government and monarchy is rare. The country ranks "Not Free" in media by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> Nonetheless, the press is not overtly hostile toward alternative viewpoints and is not restricted to publishing only articles regarding the government. The government allowed a printing and publishing company, Brunei Press PLC, to form in 1953. The company continues to print the English daily <i><a href="/wiki/Borneo_Bulletin" title="Borneo Bulletin">Borneo Bulletin</a></i>. This paper began as a weekly community paper and became a daily in 1990<sup id="cite_ref-bruneipress.com.bn_82-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bruneipress.com.bn-82">[82]</a></sup> Apart from The <i>Borneo Bulletin</i>, there is also the <i><a href="/wiki/Media_Permata" title="Media Permata">Media Permata</a></i> and Pelita Brunei, the local Malay newspapers which are circulated daily. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Brunei_Times" title="The Brunei Times">The Brunei Times</a></i> is another English independent newspaper published in Brunei since 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Brunei government owns and operates six television channels with the introduction of digital TV using DVB-T (RTB 1, RTB 2, RTB 3 (HD), RTB 4, RTB 5 and RTB New Media (Game portal)) and five radio stations (National FM, Pilihan FM, Nur Islam FM, Harmony FM and Pelangi FM). A private company has made cable television available (Astro-Kristal) as well as one private radio station, Kristal FM.<sup id="cite_ref-bruneipress.com.bn_82-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bruneipress.com.bn-82">[82]</a></sup> It also has an online campus radio station, <i><a href="/wiki/UBD_FM" title="UBD FM">UBD FM</a></i> that streams from its first university, <a href="/wiki/Universiti_Brunei_Darussalam" title="Universiti Brunei Darussalam">Universiti Brunei Darussalam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3> 
      <p>The most popular sport in Brunei is <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Brunei_national_football_team" title="Brunei national football team">Brunei national football team</a> joined <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> in 1969, but has not had much success. The top two football leagues are the <a href="/wiki/Brunei_Super_League" title="Brunei Super League">Brunei Super League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Brunei_Premier_League" title="Brunei Premier League">Brunei Premier League</a>. </p>
      <p>Brunei debuted <a href="/wiki/Brunei_at_the_Olympics" title="Brunei at the Olympics">at the Olympics</a> in 1996; it has competed at all subsequent <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> except 2008. The country has competed in badminton, shooting, swimming, and track-and-field, but is yet to win any medals. Brunei has had slightly more success <a href="/wiki/Brunei_at_the_Asian_Games" title="Brunei at the Asian Games">at the Asian Games</a>, winning four bronze medals. The first major international sporting event to be hosted in Brunei was the <a href="/wiki/1999_Southeast_Asian_Games" title="1999 Southeast Asian Games">1999 Southeast Asian Games</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/All-time_Southeast_Asian_Games_medal_table" class="mw-redirect" title="All-time Southeast Asian Games medal table">all-time Southeast Asian Games medal table</a>, Bruneian athletes have won a total of 14 gold, 55 silver and 163 bronze medals at the games. </p>

         <li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/16086/16086-h/16086-h.htm">Letter from Fajardo to Felipe III From Manila, August 15 1620. (From the Spanish Archives of the Indies)</a>("The infantry does not amount to two hundred men, in three companies. If these men were that number, and Spaniards, it would not be so bad; but, although I have not seen them, because they have not yet arrived here, I am told that they are, as at other times, for the most part boys, mestizos, and mulattoes, with some Indians (Native Americans). There is no little cause for regret in the great sums that reënforcements of such men waste for, and cost, your Majesty. I cannot see what betterment there will be until your Majesty shall provide it, since I do not think, that more can be done in Nueva Spaña, although the viceroy must be endeavoring to do so, as he is ordered.")</span> </li>

           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0896801934" title="Special:BookSources/0896801934">0896801934</a>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-151"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-151">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For a discussion of religious freedom, see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://2001-2009.state.gov/g/drl/rls/irf/2006/71334.htm">Brunei</a>.
